  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_76eb6616-12b0-4ac2-a35d-da2969af8963'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer12059575643596674757">Mum: How many stars would you give this?<br/><br/>LRN: I think a solid five. It was very good; better than the movie even. <br/><br/>Mum: So what happens in this book? <br/><br/>LRN: Soren is pushed out of his hollow by his brother, Kludd.<br/><br/>Mum: Ugh, that's an ugly name.<br/><br/>LRN: I know. <div id="review_118532145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118532145" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316545868p2/446464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118532145?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/446464-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545253062" href="/book/show/7938371-the-capture">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=tyler-and-kate-bookclub">tyler-and-kate-bookclub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=nature-animals">nature-animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/446464-kathryn?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118532145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6533805279478886187">I blush to admit that I had not head of the Lasky's series until the movie brought it to my attention. My husband and I had just finished one of Kenneth Oppel's "Silverwing" books when we saw the trailer for this adorable and very cool-looking owl movie. So, when I found out it was based on a book, it seemed only natural to transition from reading about bats to owls! ;-)<br/><br/>"The Capture" was a real surprise for me. I was expecting something cute and fun and adventuresome. Instead, I got something mu</span>
  <span id="freeText6533805279478886187" style="display:none">I blush to admit that I had not head of the Lasky's series until the movie brought it to my attention. My husband and I had just finished one of Kenneth Oppel's "Silverwing" books when we saw the trailer for this adorable and very cool-looking owl movie. So, when I found out it was based on a book, it seemed only natural to transition from reading about bats to owls! ;-)<br /><br />"The Capture" was a real surprise for me. I was expecting something cute and fun and adventuresome. Instead, I got something much more weighty and even philosophical at times. Parts of it reminded me of "The Golden Compass" and parts even brought to mind "1984" (yeah-scary!) Yeah, there are some adorable owls in this book, but there are also a lot of creepy and evil ones and they want to take over the world by brainwashing young owls. Ack! The book was also more violent than I was expecting with a few owl deaths, orphaned owls and even an owl eating another owl. Um, woah! Overall, though, it does have some humor and warmth mixed in and I thought the personalities of the owls were very well developed for such a short book. It's wonderful to watch Soren's transformation from a scared baby owl to an older owl ready to become a hero since the times call for one. I was a little annoyed that the ending was so clearly NOT resolving many of the plot threads, demanding that you read the sequels if you want to know what happens. But, even so, it did have a sense of conclusion in terms of Soren's developmental journey and intentions for the future.<br /><br />A note about the cover: I usually am not a fan of movie tie-in covers, but I just think the owl in the movie is so darn adorable I couldn't resist. However, the older cover, brown with the close-up of the owl face/eye, has really cute illustrations of the main owl characters inside the front and back cover, something the movie tie-in is sorely lacking.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6533805279478886187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_61145646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61145646" />
    <a title="L." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2277769-l"><img alt="L." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520275862p2/2277769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61145646?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L." class="user" itemprop="url" name="L." href="/user/show/2277769-l">L.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61145646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18309781674458877843">I wanted to like these books, but I didn't. I trudged through three volumes before I told my daughter that we needed to find something else to read. A few points:<br/><br/>1. The world building is inconsistent and poorly thought out. If, in this post-human world, stone castles are little more than tumbled ruins, how would any barn have survived well enough for barn owls to associate themselves with them? And why would they anyway? The inexplicable knowledge of the owls regarding human buildings is strange</span>
  <span id="freeText18309781674458877843" style="display:none">I wanted to like these books, but I didn't. I trudged through three volumes before I told my daughter that we needed to find something else to read. A few points:<br /><br />1. The world building is inconsistent and poorly thought out. If, in this post-human world, stone castles are little more than tumbled ruins, how would any barn have survived well enough for barn owls to associate themselves with them? And why would they anyway? The inexplicable knowledge of the owls regarding human buildings is strange compared to their complete lack of knowledge of humans themselves.<br /><br />2. The narcissistic belief of owl superiority over other birds, (the "wet poopers") on the part of the owls, and the zealous reverence for owls on the part of their servile nest-maid snakes, became more and more creepy with each successive book.<br /><br />3. These books could benefit from a glossary of terms and slang in the back of each. That would remove the (seeming) necessity to give up page space, better reserved for actual plot and character development, in favor of telling the reader what they already know. Just how many times does one need to be reminded what "plummels" are anyway?<br /><br />4. And if I never have to read another story-derailing, non-scanning, doggerel "battle chant" again, it will be too soon.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18309781674458877843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81262816" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81262816" />
    <a title="Cathy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526945-cathy"><img alt="Cathy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391558556p2/1526945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81262816?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy " href="/user/show/1526945-cathy">Cathy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81262816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9046028998253862060">A traditional kids-against-the-world story done in a very original way. The characters in this story are all owls. They start off very young and innocent and are forced to grow up very quickly when some evil owls take advantage of them. It turns into the beginning of an epic adventure which takes another 14 books to complete.<br/><br/>The book is a nice stepping-stone between first readers and young-adult fiction in reading difficulty, as well as in plot complexity and concepts. I think older grade school</span>
  <span id="freeText9046028998253862060" style="display:none">A traditional kids-against-the-world story done in a very original way. The characters in this story are all owls. They start off very young and innocent and are forced to grow up very quickly when some evil owls take advantage of them. It turns into the beginning of an epic adventure which takes another 14 books to complete.<br /><br />The book is a nice stepping-stone between first readers and young-adult fiction in reading difficulty, as well as in plot complexity and concepts. I think older grade school students and tweens would enjoy reading it themselves and slightly younger kids would enjoy having it read to them. I showed it to my 7 year-old and he didn't quite feel like he was up to tackling it on his own. There are some pretty serious ideas in this story, but they are introduced with minimum of fuss so I don't think kids will be disturbed. Rather, it seems like a great way for kids to start thinking about ideas like good vs. evil, overcoming fear, loyalty and even death. There is also a small amount of religious symbolism or allusion, enough to lend some grandeur to the tale but not so much as to spark that conversation unless an adult points it out.<br /><br />The friend who recommended these books to me said that they'd prompted her son into doing additional research about owls and that it's become a real area of interest for him. This book did the same for me, to some degree at least; I don't have quite the obsessive nature that an 8 year-old has about his favorite topic. But I did enjoy learning more about the various owl species in the book and was prompted to do some extra research to verify some of the information and see additional photos about these fascinating creatures. I love books that are as educational as they are fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9046028998253862060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1063217176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063217176" />
    <a title="Christina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16534594-christina"><img alt="Christina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533914761p2/16534594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063217176?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina " href="/user/show/16534594-christina">Christina </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063217176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16202114409673527420">As the Mom of a seven year old girl, I struggle to find "appropriate" books for us to read together. She reads her own books, geared toward her reading level, but we always try to have a book that I read to her on the our plate. These books are typically for older kids, but I feel exposing her to ideas and words beyond her reading level can only do her good! My struggle is... I am tired of princesses and fairies! She would never admit to it, but I have a sneaking suspicion she is tired of them t</span>
  <span id="freeText16202114409673527420" style="display:none">As the Mom of a seven year old girl, I struggle to find "appropriate" books for us to read together. She reads her own books, geared toward her reading level, but we always try to have a book that I read to her on the our plate. These books are typically for older kids, but I feel exposing her to ideas and words beyond her reading level can only do her good! My struggle is... I am tired of princesses and fairies! She would never admit to it, but I have a sneaking suspicion she is tired of them too.<br />The Capture is the perfect compromise. A book about kids (owlets) facing extreme danger and trying to solve a mystery with no help from adults (grown up owls). If fits in with my daughters need for identifiable characters and an exciting story line. I worried, at times, when I was reading this book to her, that she didn't really understand what was happening. I would finish the chapter and ask her if she still liked the book. Almost every night. <br />Her answer was always, YES! She asked questions about the characters, wondered what certain words were, and became righteously angry at a few plot points. Soren and Gylfie became friends to her. What more could I ask? Well, I could actually ask for a book that I, as an adult, would enjoy at the same time. Is that so hard? From the choices I have seen out there, apparently it is. But The Capture, pun intended, captured my interest and made me want to read each night. We are looking forward to the next book, which I hope will enthrall my daughter as much as this one has.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16202114409673527420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_110645242" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110645242" />
    <a title="Lartemis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3134450-lartemis"><img alt="Lartemis" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110645242?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lartemis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lartemis" href="/user/show/3134450-lartemis">Lartemis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110645242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer367335219965381579">I picked this book, even though it is a children's novel because I saw a preview for the movie, Guardians of Ga'Hoole. The movie has the most amazing animation, I know I'll want to see it. Often the book for these children's movies are so much better than the movie, so I decided I'd give it a whirl. After getting past the reader's various owl voices, some of which are quite overdone, I really enjoyed the book.<br/><br/>It truly is a social commentary on the world and the evil in it...and the good. Much it</span>
  <span id="freeText367335219965381579" style="display:none">I picked this book, even though it is a children's novel because I saw a preview for the movie, Guardians of Ga'Hoole. The movie has the most amazing animation, I know I'll want to see it. Often the book for these children's movies are so much better than the movie, so I decided I'd give it a whirl. After getting past the reader's various owl voices, some of which are quite overdone, I really enjoyed the book.<br /><br />It truly is a social commentary on the world and the evil in it...and the good. Much it of it reminds me of the Afghan and Iraq wars, of the Holocaust, of the Civil Rights Movement, of those we hear about on the nightly news who do evil to others and those who do good. Because of this, it is a vastly disturbing book. <br /><br />I know children in third, fourth, and fifth grade would love it and not be disturbed by it. They would see the courage, the bravery, the adventure, the scientific detail that makes the book exciting. The message of overcoming evil with courage is important and would be understood by students. It could easily lead to discussions of how to deal with bullying in schools. I love the times when, despite their obvious differences, the good owls band together, accepting the strengths of each of them and helping overcome the disabilities of each. The good owls seek to dissolve differences of class and background in order to work for the greater good.<br /><br />I'll listen to more in this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="367335219965381579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_117926388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117926388" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285872916p2/2276205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117926388?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545253062" href="/book/show/7938371-the-capture">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117926388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12196620770550408706">In anticipation of the upcoming movie based on Kathryn Lasky’s GUARDIANS OF GA’HOOLE series, Scholastic has re-released the first book in the series, <i>The Capture</i>. Being an owl fan, I of course had to give it a try! Lasky is clearly following in Richard Adams’ footsteps here, what with her invented owl words and the mixture of animal behavior and very human social commentary. <i>The Capture</i> is less intense than <i>Watership Down</i> in terms of both reading level and violence level, however, and would be s</span>
  <span id="freeText12196620770550408706" style="display:none">In anticipation of the upcoming movie based on Kathryn Lasky’s GUARDIANS OF GA’HOOLE series, Scholastic has re-released the first book in the series, <i>The Capture</i>. Being an owl fan, I of course had to give it a try! Lasky is clearly following in Richard Adams’ footsteps here, what with her invented owl words and the mixture of animal behavior and very human social commentary. <i>The Capture</i> is less intense than <i>Watership Down</i> in terms of both reading level and violence level, however, and would be suited for readers who might be too young for Adams’ book.<br /><br />Soren, our protagonist, is growing up in a loving, comfortable barn owl family. Lasky incorporates a great deal of information about owl behavior and translates it into the customs of a culture. The owls have rituals for their first bites of different types of food, for example, and for the stages of learning to fly. Lasky is skilled at depicting the intricacies of a social structure, as is evident both here and in last year’s <i>Hannah</i>. The rituals of Soren’s family create a sense of warmth and community, even if they do sometimes focus on owls’ digestive processes a little too much for me. (Kids will probably love it. Especially if they’ve done the “examine the owl pellet” thing in school.)<br /><br />One day, though, Soren tumbles from the nest and is kidnapped by several other owls. He is taken to St. Aggie’s, which claims to be a school for orphaned owls. But Soren isn’t really an orphan, and this isn’t really a school. It’s more of a cross between a totalitarian state and a cult. Now, Soren and his new friend Gylfie need to resist brainwashing, find allies, and escape St. Aggie’s. The St. Aggie’s scenes are creepy enough to get under even an adult’s skin, while still keeping the violence level appropriate for the target audience. There are a few deaths, but the details are mostly glossed over.<br /><br />Soren and Gylfie are inspired to heroism, in part, by the legends of Ga’Hoole, which are kind of like the owl equivalent of the Arthurian cycle. I really like the idea behind The Capture, which is that one should be brave in the face of tyranny and that stories can help build that courage. The book would have been stronger, though, if a few of the legends had actually been worked into the story. We often read that one character is telling the Ga’Hoole stories to another, but not what’s actually in those stories. I’ve been a mythology geek for at least twenty years, so it’s pretty easy for me to imagine what the stories are probably like, but I wouldn’t necessarily expect a child to have the same knowledge base. One of the things that worked well about Watership Down was that some of the El-ahrairah stories were included in the novel. It helped build the world the rabbits lived in, and including the stories could have done the same thing here, and it would have lent even more weight to a touching scene where Soren and Gylfie make up their own legend to honor a friend.<br /><br />Other issues include an unlikely coincidence, songs that don’t scan, and an abrupt ending. It’s not a cliffhanger, but it leaves much unresolved (presumably to be addressed in the subsequent books). This was an issue in Hannah as well, and maybe this is just a quirk of Lasky’s style that I’ll have to get used to if I continue reading her books.<br /><br />Nonetheless, <i>The Capture</i> is enjoyable for the most part, and suspenseful. The prose veers toward the “textbooky” a bit when describing owl biology and behavior, but it’s beautiful at other moments, and the story has a good message without beating you over the head with it. I’m looking forward to the movie. <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/laskykathryn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This review originally published at Fantasy Literature's Kathryn Lasky page.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12196620770550408706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer8027624902393464721">I loved the movie when I saw it, but the books had been on my to-be-read list for a long time. Now that I have read the first one, I know I will need to read them all in short order, as these books are so much better than the movie. The depth of character and the progress in the book is amazing. There is so much detail and specifics that it was wonderful to read. I am usually leery of reading books about films I liked, in part because the books are often different and you get comfortable with wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8027624902393464721" style="display:none">I loved the movie when I saw it, but the books had been on my to-be-read list for a long time. Now that I have read the first one, I know I will need to read them all in short order, as these books are so much better than the movie. The depth of character and the progress in the book is amazing. There is so much detail and specifics that it was wonderful to read. I am usually leery of reading books about films I liked, in part because the books are often different and you get comfortable with what you first experience. In this case it was a great surprise how wonderful the books were and they are so different from the movie that they are almost separate entities.<br /><br />This is the story of the Owl kingdoms, and of the classic battle between good and evil. We begin the story with a family of Owls in the nest and soon one is stolen away to a terrible place full of dark secrets. Together with a small friend, Soren escapes and soon they find themselves in a band of owls seeking out the legendary Guardians of Ga'Hoole. We watch Soren and Gylfie endure the life at St. Aggies and escape with the help of an older owl. They meet up with Twilight and Digger, two owls that could not be more different and yet they form a band and journey towards Ga'Hoole together to warn them of the evil growing at St. Aggies.<br /><br />The story was stunning, the characters amazing. You fall in love with this band of owls and cannot help but find yourself cheering them on. After you read this first one you will want the rest; it happened to me, and to the person who read book 1 after me. Looks like this book is the beginning of an exceptional series.<br /><br />Read the review and with links to other reviews of books by the author on my blog <a href="http://bit.ly/GaHoole1" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Reviews and More</a>. And also an author profile and interview with Kathryn Lasky.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8027624902393464721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17241800418209225439">I was disappointed that the book didn't really complete the story, but that's the only real fault I found. I had trouble at first with the amount of anthropomorphism in the owl characters, but they were well developed and I was quickly caught up in the story of Soren, a young owl orphaned and then kidnapped. The author made Soren's struggle to keep his identity and escape into an engaging plot that any child who has ever felt helpless and unloved will relate to.<br/><br/>The message of facing fears with c</span>
  <span id="freeText17241800418209225439" style="display:none">I was disappointed that the book didn't really complete the story, but that's the only real fault I found. I had trouble at first with the amount of anthropomorphism in the owl characters, but they were well developed and I was quickly caught up in the story of Soren, a young owl orphaned and then kidnapped. The author made Soren's struggle to keep his identity and escape into an engaging plot that any child who has ever felt helpless and unloved will relate to.<br /><br />The message of facing fears with courage and not giving up are messages I wanted my youngest son to learn. In spite of being an advanced reader who read adult level books in 6th grade,at age 16-17, he loved these books as much as I did. Perhaps more, because he usually won the contest of who got to read the next one by shutting himself in the bathroom or staying up all night.<br /><br />The author really did her research on owls. I never expected they could be so interesting or that there were so many varieties. I enjoyed the owl artwork inside the front and back covers almost as much as the story. So you know ahead,one story arc takes multiple books to complete, and each leads into the next, so don't buy just the first book or you'll go yeep. Neither my son nor I was happy when we came to the end of book 5 and didn't have 6 on hand, which ends the first story arc. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17241800418209225439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_66777744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66777744" />
    <a title="Lars Guthrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/757602-lars-guthrie"><img alt="Lars Guthrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199816668p2/757602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66777744?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lars Guthrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lars Guthrie" href="/user/show/757602-lars-guthrie">Lars Guthrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545010344" href="/book/show/774338.The_Capture">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66777744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3296676350008295319">What a pleasant surprise. I've been telling a young reader I will get to this; now that I have I wish I had done so sooner. I guess I expected something more run-of-the-mill, where Lasky's easy-to-read page-turner, about an heroic owlet who stands up to systematic thought control, is really quite profound. It makes me want to recommend 'Animal Farm' and 'Watership Down' to that young reader. And to read the next in the series. A couple of Lasky's insights:<br/><br/>'…[T:]he sweetest taste in the world…was</span>
  <span id="freeText3296676350008295319" style="display:none">What a pleasant surprise. I've been telling a young reader I will get to this; now that I have I wish I had done so sooner. I guess I expected something more run-of-the-mill, where Lasky's easy-to-read page-turner, about an heroic owlet who stands up to systematic thought control, is really quite profound. It makes me want to recommend 'Animal Farm' and 'Watership Down' to that young reader. And to read the next in the series. A couple of Lasky's insights:<br /><br />'…[T:]he sweetest taste in the world…was a question on the tongue. A word beginning with that wonderful rush of air that w’s made.<br /><br />'How do you unlearn something?...You decide not to trust only in what you can see. You look for a new way and clear your mind of the old way. You try to feel new things….'<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3296676350008295319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1816136380" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816136380" />
    <a title="Amy (won&#39;t be online for a while. sorry to all the groups i&#39;m in!)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60014615-amy-won-t-be-online-for-a-while-sorry-to-all-the-groups-i-m-in"><img alt="Amy (won&#39;t be online for a while. sorry to all the groups i&#39;m in!)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510119624p2/60014615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1816136380?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy (won&#39;t be online for a while. sorry to all the groups i&#39;m in!)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy (won&#39;t be online for a while. sorry to all the groups i&#39;m in!)" href="/user/show/60014615-amy-won-t-be-online-for-a-while-sorry-to-all-the-groups-i-m-in">Amy (won&#39;t be online for a while. sorry to all the groups i&#39;m in!)</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1816136380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17927452057756464005">Have you ever wondered what it would feel like to be abducted? How would you feel if you went looking for your family and they weren’t there? That is what happened to a little owl named Soren and thousands of other hatchlings before him! What’s next?<br/><br/>The Capture, book one in The Guardians of Ga’Hoole series written by Kathryn Lasky, is a fantasy novel. This book introduces the reader to a parliament of owls. Included in this group are Soren, Gylfie, Digger, and Twilight. The story begins with a l</span>
  <span id="freeText17927452057756464005" style="display:none">Have you ever wondered what it would feel like to be abducted? How would you feel if you went looking for your family and they weren’t there? That is what happened to a little owl named Soren and thousands of other hatchlings before him! What’s next?<br /><br />The Capture, book one in The Guardians of Ga’Hoole series written by Kathryn Lasky, is a fantasy novel. This book introduces the reader to a parliament of owls. Included in this group are Soren, Gylfie, Digger, and Twilight. The story begins with a little barn owl named Soren falling to the ground and being snatched up and taken from his family. He is brought to St Aegolius Academy for Orphaned Owls even though he was not orphaned! It is at this orphanage where he meets a little Elf owl named Gylfie, his soon to be best friend. Soren and Gylfie resisted being moon blinked and began looking for others like them. In the search they found Hortense and Grimble. Through stories from Grimble they discover a great evil plan. Grimble’s hope returned and he helped these young hatchlings to fly in secret in hopes of helping them escape. They were successful in their escape but this was to Grimble’s demise. Soren and Gylfie’s search for the legend begins. Will they become part of the legend or will they become heroes?<br /><br />Kathryn Lasky, the author of The Capture, was able to develop this story through character interaction, personality development and conflict, of course. The book unfolded at a perfect pace for the reader to stay interested and has many parts that will make you not want to put the book down. The author’s craft of developing characters is exquisite. She developed her characters through interactions, dialogue, internal thoughts and their response to situations. The two characters who I related to the most were Soren and Gylfie. As the reader, I saw Soren grow both in confidence and knowledge. The author was able to show this in a variety of ways. The author used Soren’s knowledge of the Ga’hoolian legends to help to save both Soren and Gylfie as shown on page 94 where he begins talking to Gylfie so that they do not fall asleep to not get moon blinked. When Soren is learning to fly he demonstrated his confidence by saying “I can do it, I can do it! I feel the air. I feel the force of my strokes. I am going up. I am going up. I shall fly…”(pg.155). <br /><br />Gylfie could be described as a caring, intelligent, encouraging leader. The author was able to portray those characteristics through dialogue and situations. We learn that Gylfie is quite smart when she is able to convince Soren to pretend to march so they do not get moon blinked (p.56). Lasky also showed Gylfie’s leadership through her interactions with Grimble, especially when questioning him about faking being moon blinked. She took charge of this and went forward even though Soren was scared (p.141). <br /><br />The author made me loath the evil owls of Saint Aggies with a fiery passion because of what they did with the little owls that they snatched. The two owls I did make the exception for were Grimble and Hortense. Hortense’s character was actually quite nice and there was something mysterious about her. Grimble’s character became Soren and Gylfie accomplice and has a big part in their escape from Saint Aggies! Kathryn Lasky’s use of vivid words helped to create realistic, dramatic images in my mind. From how she described the characters, the incidences and the places they traveled I felt like I was on the same journey with them. I was rooting for them to succeed.<br /> <br />I really loved this book because I found every chapter that I read would get me thinking about what would happen next to these little owl! The author, Kathryn Lasky was able to build suspense with her use of vivid words, language and dialogue. She was able to make me feel joy, anger, excitement and sadness as she developed the characters and the story. The Capture began with fear, as Soren was trying to get back to his hollow “He was in trouble - deep, frightening, horrifying trouble.”(p.16) and ended with hope “They must warn of the evil that threatened. They must become part of this ancient kingdom of knights on silent wings who rose in the blackness to perform deeds of greatness” (p.218). It was through determination and belief in self and others that this parliament of owls are able to continue their journey towards the great Tree of Ga’Hoole in the sea of Hoolemere.<br /><br />There is a large variety in the fantasy genre. The Capture was a great way to begin the series of the Guardians of Ga’Hoole. I would highly recommend this book to those who enjoy reading animal fantasy novels. If you enjoy reading books that have a little bit of murder, mystery, adventure and fantasy this would be a good place to start. Although the ending is not clear for those young owls the author tempts you to keep reading the series. You are left with one question which encourages you to read on to find out if the legend is true.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17927452057756464005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_120329825" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120329825" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/327471-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188525077p2/327471.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120329825?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/327471-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545253062" href="/book/show/7938371-the-capture">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327471-kristen?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327471-kristen?shelf=middlegrade">middlegrade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120329825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3329333458943724307">Why I read this: When I heard this was being turned into a movie, I figured it was time to read it. We have the series at my school library and when I got offered a new cool looking paperback from the publisher, I dug right into it.<br/><br/>Plot: Amazing. Definitely a great start to what is now a 13 book series (WOW, what have I gotten myself into?) and I can see that this series will be full of adventure. I felt like the pacing was right on and definitely a great adventure that my students will be diggi</span>
  <span id="freeText3329333458943724307" style="display:none">Why I read this: When I heard this was being turned into a movie, I figured it was time to read it. We have the series at my school library and when I got offered a new cool looking paperback from the publisher, I dug right into it.<br /><br />Plot: Amazing. Definitely a great start to what is now a 13 book series (WOW, what have I gotten myself into?) and I can see that this series will be full of adventure. I felt like the pacing was right on and definitely a great adventure that my students will be digging into. I'm actually going to set up a display for series this month around the time the movie comes out and will be proud to say I've read at least one so far. Back to the plot for a minute though - this book was a great starter - you follow Soren through where he came from and to the orphanage that will change his life forever. I love the sense of adventure and I really couldn't put this down for long.<br /><br />Characters: Soren is a great main character. He's not your typical hero - he's smarter than the average owl but is definitely not the brazen type. Soren is smart and it shows in how he reacts to situations - he's careful and thinks things through - not just plowing in and hoping all goes well. He's really young too and has a lot more bravery inside of him than I think really shines through.<br /><br />His sidekick Gylfie is a small Elf Owl who helps him realize he's right about something being wrong at St. Aegolius'. I really loved how Gylfie used long vocabulary and really was not the typical owl either. I can't wait to see more of these two in the rest of the series. I may be bringing the next one home from work tomorrow. :)<br /><br />Relatability: I think my students could really relate to this book in many different ways. There's a sense of adventure throughout the book, but also the characters have their flaws and are very relatable. They really are young characters and it's nice to see smaller characters prevail in novels.<br /><br />Cover Commentary: I love the movie cover - especially the blue colors. Definitely a book my students will want to pick up.<br /><br /><br />Read more: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookworminginthe21stcentury.com/search/label/review#ixzz0zEJ0rd34">http://www.bookworminginthe21stcentur...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3329333458943724307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8006185023891471576" style="display:none">Reviewed by Joan Stradling for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Born in the peaceful forest of Tyto, Soren the barn owl looks forward to a life of eating bugs and learning to fly, but evil forces have another plan for the owls.<br /><br />When Soren is captured and taken to a mysterious place known as St. Aegolius Academy for Orphaned Owls, he discovers the orphanage has a darker purpose. With the help of his friend, Gylfie, they set out to uncover the truth and find a way to escape.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the only way out is up, and the young owls will have to learn to fly if they have a hope of escape.<br /><br />I first read THE CAPTURE many years ago and looked forward to reacquainting myself with the world of the owls. This tale of suspense and finding heroes in unlikely places is full of struggles and triumphs that are easy to relate to, even though the main characters are birds. Re-reading it made me want to get my hands on the other books in the GUARDIANS OF GA'HOOLE series so I can continue reading Soren's story. </span>

Her characters, despite being owls, are extremely well developed and each has a distinct personality.   <span id="freeText2566786226050206700" style="display:none">Like Watership Down, i doubted how enjoyable i would find a book told from the perspective of animals. Her characters, despite being owls, are extremely well developed and each has a distinct personality. The plot is exciting and there is plenty of action and adventure to please both young and older readers. It's not a very long book, but the quality of the writing is extremely high. <br />Highly recommended. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2500814618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2500814618" />
    <a title="Annie (Putt)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47291796-annie-putt"><img alt="Annie (Putt)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582160152p2/47291796.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2500814618?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie (Putt)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie (Putt)" href="/user/show/47291796-annie-putt">Annie (Putt)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2500814618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6625571982380861513">The Capture is a great way to set up the world of the owls without info dumping all of the world on us at once.  Since we are following the journey of Soren, we learn about places as he does, which makes sense because at the beginning of the series, he would be the equivalent of a seven year old child.  He doesn't understand what concepts such as "weeks" or "years" are because he's only been alive for maybe twenty days.<br/><br/>Soren's struggle with St. Aggie's and growing up into a darker world that his</span>
  <span id="freeText6625571982380861513" style="display:none">The Capture is a great way to set up the world of the owls without info dumping all of the world on us at once.  Since we are following the journey of Soren, we learn about places as he does, which makes sense because at the beginning of the series, he would be the equivalent of a seven year old child.  He doesn't understand what concepts such as "weeks" or "years" are because he's only been alive for maybe twenty days.<br /><br />Soren's struggle with St. Aggie's and growing up into a darker world that his parents had shown him was a culture shock, and one I'm certain a lot of kids and teens can agree with.  Those children whose parents have died or left them with no warning, or parents who remarried awful people all would identify with Soren and his constant wish to go back 'to how it used to be.'  But you can't.  No one can.  When catastrophic events happen in life, there is no going back, and Soren begins to learn this through his stay at St. Aggies.<br /><br />I love that the focus of not just this book but the entire series is the friendships.  In this one, specifically Soren and Gylfie and then later with Twilight and Digger joining their band.  The friendships in this are what make the characters stronger, and they compliment each other.  Soren has his talents in thinking deeply and with his heart, and Gylfie is cunning and able to sneak around.  Both are highly intelligent owls, but more than that, it's less that they're geniuses and more that they actually bother to think, whereas most people go with the status quo, Soren and Gylfie played along and watched the world around them.<br /><br />Soren starts out as a slight buffoon, which can be forgiven as he's a child.  He begins to mature, and the more he let's himself consider those deep things of the heart and soul, the wiser he grows.  He starts considering what St. Aggies means to not just himself or Gylfie, but to his homeland and the owl kingdoms.<br /><br />Gylfie, too, understands the issues with St. Aggies, and while she may not be able to consider as well the moral implications behind the things that happen, she's shrewd in her observations and able to understand that things have to change.<br /><br />One reason this book is so enjoyable is the fact that there is less telling than showing.  When Gylfie or Soren show up to tell the other what happened, they proceed to go back and test out the theories again.  You watch them learn to fly.  You see them watch the horrors of St. Aggies.  You were there when Soren was snatched.  You don't find out about this later on.<br /><br />Highly recommended if not for the story, then for the power of friendship theme throughout.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6625571982380861513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1971856552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971856552" />
    <a title="Haley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51352764-haley"><img alt="Haley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511845066p2/51352764.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1971856552?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haley" href="/user/show/51352764-haley">Haley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786029698725" href="/book/show/8667908-the-capture">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51352764-haley?shelf=04-2017">04-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1971856552&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971856552" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7945416659762901269">I usually don't read middle school books, but I just happened to have this on my shelf the same time a buddy read was going on for it. I did like this book more than I thought I would, but it still was a little too childish for me. This book is about a barn owl, Soren being pushed from his nest at a young age by his brother. He is taken from his home only to find himself in an orphanage with other owls. He doesn't know what to think of it at first especially when given a new name, 121 and told n</span>
  <span id="freeText7945416659762901269" style="display:none">I usually don't read middle school books, but I just happened to have this on my shelf the same time a buddy read was going on for it. I did like this book more than I thought I would, but it still was a little too childish for me. This book is about a barn owl, Soren being pushed from his nest at a young age by his brother. He is taken from his home only to find himself in an orphanage with other owls. He doesn't know what to think of it at first especially when given a new name, 121 and told never to ask questions or there will be consequences. While there he meets up with other owl whos name is Gylfie and they plan a way to break out of the orphanage. This is the entirety of the plot and it's sweet seeing how the owls plan together to find a way to learn how to fly, figure out what is happening all to escape. They plan to find their parents when out only to find out that their families are gone. They meet up with other owls who are alone and orphans and head their way to Ga'hoole. I will be continuing this series just because it's a cute little series. </span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('b2p8xczQS/rIdkW5zHOvoOcfhzO49yBu4dRB00YalnDgt730qMErrCzXZYqMHJ9CwV6u1xPc/HVsV1onDgWyTw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+n95lxq9pByD8xrw8krnnPAy7od0pleWuw/bpiZ8e9Z1orimfqzESmdSOsOyJdd+1nPHY9+Ni402jMBSbmNf6Q==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4735.Kathryn_Lasky">About Kathryn Lasky</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4735.Kathryn_Lasky"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1324072694p3/4735.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8414052840313946305"><i>Kathryn Lasky</i> is the American author of many critically acclaimed books, including several Dear America books, several Royal Diaries books, 1984 Newbery Honor winning <i>Sugaring Time, The Night Journey</i>, and the <i>Guardians of Ga'Hoole</i> series.<br/><br/>She was born June 24, 1944, and grew up in Indianapolis, Indiana, and is married to Christopher Knight, with whom she lives in Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Book 15,<i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3301645.The_War_of_the_Ember' title='The War of the Ember' rel='nofollow noopener'>The War of t</a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText8414052840313946305" style="display:none"><i>Kathryn Lasky</i> is the American author of many critically acclaimed books, including several Dear America books, several Royal Diaries books, 1984 Newbery Honor winning <i>Sugaring Time, The Night Journey</i>, and the <i>Guardians of Ga'Hoole</i> series.<br /><br />She was born June 24, 1944, and grew up in Indianapolis, Indiana, and is married to Christopher Knight, with whom she lives in Massachusetts.<br /><br />Book 15,<i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3301645.The_War_of_the_Ember" title="The War of the Ember" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Ember</a></i>, is currently the last book in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40440-guardians-of-ga-hoole" rel="nofollow noopener">Ga'Hoole series</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17166341.The_Rise_of_a_Legend" title="The Rise of a Legend" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rise of a Legend</a> is the 16th book but is a prequel to the series. Lasky has also written <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/774337.Guide_Book_To_The_Great_Tree" title="Guide Book To The Great Tree" rel="nofollow noopener">Guide Book To The Great Tree</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7209860.Lost_Tales_Of_Ga_Hoole" title="Lost Tales Of Ga'Hoole" rel="nofollow noopener">Lost Tales Of Ga'Hoole</a> which are companion books.</span>
